Page 23

1933.02.19

Geneva Cables Express Resolve to Resist; League of Nations Places Great Importance on It; Song Delivers Stirring Speech at Welcome Reception 1

(Geneva) Zhang Xueliang, Commander-in-Chief of the Northeastern Army, together with Song Ziwen, Acting President of the Executive Yuan, have recently arrived in Rehe and sent a telegram to the Chinese delegation in Geneva, which reads as follows: "The Chinese government and people have resolved to resist Japanese aggression and are now concentrating their forces to defend our territory. I and President Song have arrived in the capital of Rehe Province. The purpose of this trip is to complete the defense plan so that China's territorial integrity will not be subjected to constant Japanese threats. The Chinese government has previously endured humiliation and worked hard for a long time in the hope of sincerely preventing the situation from worsening, so that the League of Nations could find a basis for mediation in accordance with the Covenant and other treaties. However, the hope of mediation has been severed by Japan, and the hope of peace has been destroyed by Japan's military actions in Rehe, despite the League of Nations' serious objections, which are ignored. Japan's specious reasons for occupying Manchuria were to maintain treaty rights, but Japan's invasion of Rehe cannot be justified by this excuse, as no treaty involves this province. We have received orders from the central government to resist Japanese aggression and have the responsibility to defend our territory, which is supported by the people of the North. Please explain our position and attitude to the League of Nations and the world." This telegram has been translated and sent to the Secretariat of the League of Nations. (Havas Dispatch, 18th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations attaches great importance to Zhang Xueliang and Song Ziwen's arrival in Rehe, believing that China has long been determined to resist Japan. Although Japan has threatened to withdraw from the League of Nations, no one here believes that Japan will actually do so. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

Chengde 2

Song Ziwen, accompanied by Zhang Xueliang and Zhang Zuoxiang, arrived in Chengde. Song delivered a speech at the welcome reception, saying, "I, Ziwen, have been ordered to come north and have consulted with Acting Chairman Zhang and others in Peiping on resisting the enemy. Yesterday, I came to Rehe with Acting Chairman Zhang and Chief Commander Zhang to inspect the situation. I am extremely grateful to Chairman Tang and the military and civilian leaders for holding a meeting to welcome me. As a member of the nation and a member of the government, I feel it is my duty to work harder when the country is in crisis. This trip north, and my conversations with local people, have further convinced me that the defense of North China depends entirely on Rehe as a shield. Protecting Rehe is the only way to protect North China, and it also gives hope for the recovery of the lost three eastern provinces. If Rehe is lost, North China will be shaken, and the impact will be felt throughout the country. After observing the situation in Chengde, I feel even more the importance of Rehe, and the morale of the troops at the front and the indignation of the people in the rear are enough to inspire me. Now the Committee of Nineteen of the League of Nations has conducted a very detailed study and unanimously supports China's position. Although the Japanese militarists are strong and violent, they cannot resist the whole world with one country. Therefore, the final victory will belong to us, but we must still work hard ourselves and not rely entirely on others. The Japanese militarists will soon launch an offensive. Although our weapons and equipment are far inferior to theirs, with the consistent policy of our national government and people, and the consistent public opinion, our armed compatriots will sacrifice their precious lives at the front, and our national people will contribute money and effort in the rear. The final victory will belong to us. I, Ziwen, have already written to the generals at the front, stating that the national crisis is pressing. This is not the time for us to talk leisurely. I can only say briefly, I am willing to offer a million points of sincerity and advise all sectors of the country to eliminate prejudices, unite as one, and work hard to resist the enemy. I will also follow behind you, and as long as I am in office, I will fulfill my duty. All my compatriots in the country should take this to heart." (Special Dispatch, 18th)

(Peiping) People here believe that the international situation in China has never been as serious as it is today since the Boxer Rebellion, regarding the impending war in Rehe Province. Although war has not yet been declared, the situation of war has already been formed. The Chinese and Japanese soldiers no longer have any differences of opinion, but are only waiting for battle. Finance Minister Song's visit to Peiping has greatly strengthened people's hearts and repeatedly stated that the whole country is willing to be the backing for the war of resistance against Japan, not just the battle of a corner of the northern military and people. This kind of frankness has long been hoped for. Now, talking with the responsible Chinese in the north, they do not show any signs of fanaticism, but only have a calm, firm determination to resist to the end. Public opinion is that the League of Nations has done its best and has given China a spiritual victory with its moral authority. The League of Nations can do nothing more than this. Now we can only rely on China to use its physical strength to fight for it. This kind of strength is what the League of Nations does not have. Peiping is still very peaceful, but the public feels that a tragic war will break out in a week or so. According to news from the three eastern provinces, the Japanese military's preparations have been completed, and Mutō's army is only waiting for the final hour to arrive. The Chinese side has also amassed a large army to prepare for resistance, including the volunteer army, totaling about 150,000 people. They are now waiting for the enemy's attack, and it is said that they are fully supplied with bullets. According to visitors from Rehe Province, the Chinese army is defending by relying on dangerous terrain, which is very advantageous. If the Rehe provincial army can show the same determination as the 19th Route Army in the Battle of Shanghai a year ago, then the Japanese military's plan to capture Chengde within a week seems likely to be thwarted. If the Chinese army's fighting ability is equal to its determination, then Rehe Province will become a thrilling battlefield, and the Battle of Shanghai last year was like military exercises. (Reuters Dispatch, 18th)

Chengde 3

Military and civilian leaders from all parts of Rehe have gathered here to welcome Zhang Xueliang, Song Ziwen, and Zhang Zuoxiang. Zhang and others came here to complete the plan to resist the Japanese army's continued attack on Rehe. Today, the whole city is flying flags to show respect. Officials and people are extremely excited. Song Ziwen gave a speech to the public, which was extremely impassioned. At the end, he said that he represented the central government in declaring to the public that the national government would never give up the Northeast and never give up Rehe. Even if the enemy occupies Nanjing, no one will be willing to sign a treaty of surrender. (Reuters Dispatch, 18th)

The League of Nations Assembly Opens on Monday, A Head-On Collision with Japan is Inevitable

Chairman Hymans Announces Failure of Mediation, Proceeds with Fourth Item Procedure; Japanese Cabinet Decides to First Recall Geneva Representatives and Consider Withdrawal from the League 4

The United States Does Not Make Formal Statement on League of Nations Recommendations for the Time Being

(Geneva) Chairman Hymans announced today that the League of Nations Assembly will open on Tuesday and issued a formal communiqué stating that all efforts to mediate the Sino-Japanese dispute have failed. Therefore, the Assembly must now proceed with its responsibilities under Article 15, Paragraph 4 of the Covenant and discuss the sanctions provided for under Article 16. The Chinese and Japanese representatives will speak first on that day. It is expected that the final vote can be taken on Friday. Neither the Chinese nor the Japanese representatives have the right to vote.

Judging from the news from Tokyo, the break between Japan and the League of Nations is only a matter of time, or perhaps just a matter of time. The League of Nations is not surprised by this, as it has already expected this result from the Manchurian proposal. Today's question is whether the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference can survive this shock. Since Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, it is feared that it will also withdraw its representatives from the Disarmament Conference. Everyone feels that we should now find ways to increase the League of Nations' declining prestige, but the plans are diverse and we do not know which to follow. In addition to the Manchurian proposal, the gap between certain countries is now also becoming wider. (National Telegram, 18th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly is scheduled to meet next Tuesday to consider the report of the Committee of Nineteen on the Sino-Japanese dispute. The understanding of the nature of its agenda is gradually taking shape. The important task is to formally record the provisions of Articles 15(3) to 15(4) of the League of Nations Covenant. It is unlikely that there will be a vote, but Chairman Hymans will make a statement explaining the overall situation and confirming that the recommendations made to Japan have been rejected, so the mediation procedure has failed. It is then expected that the Chinese and Japanese representatives will be asked to express their opinions. It is now believed that the Chinese representative has prepared a declaration, but the will of the Japanese side is still unclear. It is said that several members of the Assembly have opposed postponing the meeting on Tuesday to Friday. According to the rules of procedure of the meeting, at least two days' notice must be given before the next meeting can be convened, so the current procedure will not be changed. The responsibilities of the Committee of Nineteen have now legally come to an end. If further service is requested, there are organizational law concerns. It is said that the Swiss representative has stated that he does not wish to serve on the Committee of Nineteen. The acting chairman is now considering appointing a new committee in accordance with Article 3 of the League of Nations Covenant, but jurists here doubt whether this move requires unanimous consent. It is said that Hymans will come here from Brussels at the end of this week. (Reuters Dispatch, 18th)

Full Text of Report Released Today

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Rushes Translation Day and Night; Totaling Over 20,000 Words, Will Be Printed into a Special Booklet 5

(Nanjing) The report of the Committee of Nineteen of the League of Nations was broadcast to the world by the Geneva Radio Station on the afternoon of the 17th. The Chinese Zhenru International Radio Station followed up and transferred it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received all of it from 3:00 pm on the 17th to 6:00 am on the 18th, totaling 85 pages and over 15,000 words. At the same time, the Central News Agency and Reuters also received the full text from Shanghai. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs worked all night on the 17th to sort out the telegrams, and began translating them at 8:00 am on the 18th, under the direction of Li Dijun, Director of the Information Department. The entire translation was completed by 5:00 pm, totaling over 20,000 words. Foreign Minister Luo and Vice Minister Xu personally reviewed it, and it was started to be written at 8:00 pm, and it could be fully announced by 12:00 pm that night. The English original will also be mimeographed and published, and the translation will be broadcast nationwide by the Central News Agency. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will reorganize it after the League of Nations Assembly approves the report and print it into a booklet. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 18th)

(Nanjing) The general report of the Committee of Nineteen of the League of Nations, broadcast by the Geneva Radio Station, has been collected by the Zhenru Radio Station and telegraphed to Beijing. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs received it at 11:00 pm on the 18th and immediately typed it in English, totaling more than 90 pages. In the afternoon, personnel were dispatched to speed up the translation, which could be completed that night. It will be mimeographed and published on the 19th morning and sent to Chairman Lin, Chairman Chiang, and the heads of various ministries and commissions, and Chinese and English pamphlets will be printed for all sectors to read. (Special Dispatch, 18th)

(Geneva) The full text of the report of the Committee of Nineteen has been published. People in the League of Nations are paying particular attention to the last paragraph, which states that the major powers of the League of Nations reserve the right to continue to take concerted action after consulting with each other and with non-member states. It is said that this means that the League of Nations will ignore Japan's protests and seek the opinions of the United States and Russia on this matter. (National Telegram, 18th)

The United States is Satisfied with the League of Nations Report

Content Matches Hoover's Doctrine 6

(Forceful Statement to be Made After Roosevelt Takes Office)

(Washington) Today, the US government has received the full text of the Committee of Nineteen's Manchurian proposal report and recommendations. The State Department is currently considering it and has made no statement. It is reported that the content of the report is actually consistent with President Hoover's policies in all aspects, and the recommendation to recognize China's basic sovereignty in Manchuria and the section on maintaining treaties are particularly in line with the US attitude. However, because the US government is about to change, and US officials also want world public opinion to be fully influenced by the report without any other opinions mixed in to distract the world and increase its complexity, they do not want to make any comments for the time being. Informal comments mostly claim that the report, which represents world opinion, is a promising sign that a satisfactory solution to the Manchurian proposal can be achieved in the end. The report will now be copied and sent to President-elect Roosevelt for review. Even if it is generally consistent with the intentions expressed by Wilson, it is expected that the US government will wait for Roosevelt to express his opinion before issuing a formal comment, and only after Roosevelt and Stimson have discussed it will it be possible to issue a formal statement. Roosevelt has not yet directly commented on the Manchurian proposal, only saying that the sanctity of treaties must be maintained. At present, people are speculating whether Roosevelt will mention this matter in his inaugural address on March 4. Chairman Borah of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee stated that the content of the report is what the world has a right to expect, but he believes that Japan will be unwilling for the League of Nations to take any action and will continue to implement its already announced plan. The United States is now waiting for the League of Nations' final action on this report. (National Telegram, 17th)

(Washington) The State Department stated today that whether the United States will participate in the League of Nations mediation committee for the Sino-Japanese dispute will be decided by Roosevelt after he takes office as president. It is also said that Senator Claude may be the new chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee. Today, it is claimed that the League of Nations report is too detailed to be criticized immediately, and it is not appropriate to announce a policy towards Manchuria without the decision of the new president. (Reuters Dispatch, 18th)

The World Society translated Miller's Commentary report, saying, "How the Roosevelt government, which is about to take office, will deal with the Far East crisis cannot be known until the new president actually takes office and appoints a new Secretary of State. Until now, the leaders of the new government have only declared that their policies will not undergo fundamental changes and will continue Hoover and Stimson's policy of not recognizing Japan's acquisition of land based on the destruction of treaties. A person familiar with Washington's political situation recently wrote to this newspaper, and his words are recorded below: 'The United States' policy towards China is not a matter of Republican or Democratic policy, but a traditional policy that every government inherits without any substantive changes. But it must be known that Hoover and Roosevelt currently disagree on various issues. After the new government takes office, it may depart from the regulations of the previous government, which is natural. The attitudes of the two parties towards the Kellogg-Briand Pact during the election campaign were somewhat similar. Roosevelt has not yet expressed his opinion on the Japanese issue. People here are quite sorry that the Japanese are using an article written by Roosevelt after the Washington Conference in 1922 for propaganda. It must be known that the situation has changed greatly in the ten years since this article was written. In general, the Democratic Party is more friendly to the League of Nations, but it is too early to make any predictions based on this point. As far as the Democratic Party is concerned, it has less courage to adopt any policies that could lead to war. Some people predict that Roosevelt will be more friendly to China than Hoover, because Hoover was in Tianjin during the Boxer Rebellion and is therefore inevitably prejudiced. At present, a Democratic Party leader of a country, under the guidance of Roosevelt, is engaged in a serious and informal study of the Far Eastern situation in preparation for the new president's use after taking office. Domestic affairs and economic issues, war debts, and the International Economic Conference will take precedence over the Manchurian issue. There is a hope, often expressed among both Democrats and Republicans, that Japan will eventually collapse economically, so that the powers will be spared from taking any strong actions that could lead to dangerous situations.'"

(Washington) After studying the recommendations of the Committee of Nineteen, American legal experts stated today that whether the United States will participate in the actions that the League of Nations Assembly will take on the Manchurian proposal will largely depend on whether a US-Manchurian mechanism can be established to protect China's sovereignty and Japan's legitimate interests. These experts seem to agree with the report's statement that Japan's interests are facts that cannot be ignored, but on the one hand, these interests must be protected, while at the same time, full compliance with all treaties relating to this dispute must be insisted upon, which is a most tangled problem. The State Department must first resolve this before it can state the United States' position. The US government may not make a formal statement before the League of Nations takes final action on the report, but senators have already begun to discuss the report, and it appears that a large portion will oppose the United States' participation in a movement to put pressure on Japan, and many senators say that Japan will fully concede to allow negotiations to begin. It was also recently learned that President-elect Roosevelt will not have the opportunity to study the recommendations of the Committee of Nineteen for several days because of a prior appointment with a New York Democratic Party leader. (National News Agency Telegram, 17th)

Lytton Makes Important Statement Opposing Warfare to Safeguard Peace

Sanction Methods Should Be Decided by the Government 7

(London) Lord Lytton spoke today at Albert Hall in Manchester, referring to the remarks he made at a banquet of the Japanese Student Association in London last Tuesday night, saying, "Part of my speech to the Japanese Student Association on Tuesday has been disclosed by some London newspapers. Now I would like to make a slight statement on this. The banquet that night was a private gathering, and there were no reporters present. Although I do not object to the publication of my remarks, because what I said can be heard by the world, the way my remarks were relayed gave people an incorrect impression of what I said. During the banquet, people asked various questions, which I answered one by one. The person who published my remarks strung together my answers to various questions, leading readers to mistakenly believe that this was a coherent speech, while the questions asked to me at the time were deleted. I do not blame others for saying that I said something that I did not say, but the impression created by this news is that I expressed the opinion that if the League of Nations Assembly report is disregarded, then the League of Nations will no longer be able to take other actions. In fact, this is not my opinion, which is why I want to take this opportunity to correct this impression. If either party refuses to accept the assistance offered by the League of Nations and acts in a way that violates the Covenant, then the resources available to the League of Nations are not exhausted. I did express that I do not consider warfare to safeguard peace as a remedy. I did say that a worldwide economic blockade cutting off Japan's various exports would punish innocent civilians rather than the arrogant government, so it would be severe and could provoke a real state of war. But there are many other means of pressure that can be exercised, such as prohibiting the sale of munitions to the breaching country, or refusing financial assistance, or withdrawing diplomatic representatives. I am not saying that any of the above steps should be implemented now or at any time, because the timing and manner of exercising this pressure must be decided by the responsible government. I only want to make it clear that I am not saying that the above methods are not necessary methods that can be taken when necessary." (Reuters Dispatch, 17th)

Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs Cables Matsuoka

Return to Country Via Siberia 8

(Tokyo) According to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Japanese government has completed the procedures for withdrawing from the League of Nations. After yesterday's emergency cabinet meeting, in addition to ordering Japanese representatives Matsuoka, Nagaoka, and Sato to make a final tough break speech at the 25th Assembly, Matsuoka Yosuke was also ordered to return to the country via Siberia as soon as possible after the Assembly speech in order to report on the proceedings at the meeting of senior ministers and decide to formally withdraw from the League of Nations. (China United Press, 18th)

Current Affairs Commentary

The So-Called "Ultimatum" Appears Only After One and a Half Years of War 9

— Hui

(1) Proposals After the Nineteen-Nation Committee Suggestion

Since the League of Nations' Nineteen-Nation Committee put forward its proposals, the Japanese government has shown alarm, while the military has roared, believing that it should immediately withdraw from the League of Nations, implement its dreamed-of Monroe Doctrine of Asia, and carry out its "continental policy" to achieve the goals of annexing the three northeastern provinces and invading North China. This time, the Nineteen-Nation Committee's proposal does not recognize the Japanese army's violence in Shenyang on September 18th of the previous year as self-defense, and also suggests that League member states not recognize the "made-in-Japan puppet" 丨 "Manchukuo." The sincerity of its advocacy of "fairness" is especially worthy of our praise. However, there is no clear stipulation on the time and procedure for the withdrawal of the Japanese army. The territorial sovereignty of the three northeastern provinces should be restored first, otherwise it will eventually be a "flower in a mirror," with no power to implement it. Moreover, the League of Nations is only a moral sanctioning body, how can it make the Japanese warlords necessarily obey? Therefore, at a minimum, Article 16 of the Covenant must be used for economic blockade, so that Japanese militarists still know that the world has "fairness and justice," and that the nations can ultimately not be deceived, and China cannot be humiliated.

However, the Japanese cliques are strong and tyrannical by nature, relying on force both internally and externally. They not only want to annex "Manchuria" but also forcibly occupy Yuguan and garrison troops on the border of Liaoning and Rehe, and yet shamelessly praise themselves for maintaining peace in the Far East. In fact, it is the iron hand of Japan that is destroying peace in the Far East. It is also the Japanese warlords who are tearing up all international conventions. All enlightened people in the world recognize the violence of Japanese imperialism and feel injustice on behalf of our country. Although the incident has been delayed until now, from Liaoning and Jilin in northern Manchuria to Jinzhou and Yi County, and now even disaster has befallen Yuguan with the bombing of Rehe, on the one hand, it is due to the instability of the international political situation, and on the other hand, it is because our country has no real strength to support "fairness and justice." Therefore, the Japanese cabinet is allowed to act recklessly without restraint.

What is even worse is that the Japanese army is taking an inch and wanting a mile, provoking in Yuguan and demonstrating on the Rehe border, and even publicly stating that they will begin to attack Rehe on the 27th of this month, and that a large-scale battle will begin on March 1st. This is because March 1st is the anniversary of the Japanese army's creation of the ""Manchukuo puppet state." Therefore, the so-called "ultimatum" is prepared. The first one is sent by the so-called "Manchurian" government to Tang Yulin, the chairman of Rehe Province. The second one is sent by Muto Nobuyoshi, the commander of the Kwantung Army, to Zhang Xueliang, the chief of the three northeastern provinces in Beiping. The third one is sent by the Japanese government to the National Government. The wording is (Japan) strongly demands that Chinese troops withdraw from Rehe, because they believe that Rehe is "Manchurian" land. What is this! The Japanese militarist aggression is thus exposed without any disguise.

(2) Strange Statements from Japan

Japan has long had a dual diplomacy externally and a dual government internally. However, since the September 18th Incident, it has become even more obvious that the so-called Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the so-called Cabinet are merely echo chambers of the military, just like puppets. Therefore, whenever an incident occurs (especially those related to China-Japan affairs and the Northeast issue, involving international relations), the Japanese military must issue a strange statement to express the Japanese cliques' aggressive consciousness and their external strength. This time, the League of Nations Nineteen-Nation Committee declared responsibility, believing that the Manchukuo puppet was actually created by the Japanese cliques' army and has nothing to do with the 30 million people of the Northeast. Therefore, the Japanese army authorities issued another statement, believing that "Japan's recognition of 'Manchuria' is its national policy, and the attack on Rehe is not allowed to be interfered with by the League of Nations. Now that the League of Nations has rejected Japan's proposal and is questioning Japan, making it difficult for Japan, Japan has no need to answer. It is appropriate to immediately withdraw from the League of Nations."

What is even stranger is that Muto, the commander of the Kwantung Army, also issued a statement: "First, he praised the (puppet) 'Manchuria' he created. Second, he stated that the nations are gradually understanding the true meaning of the so-called kingdom of righteousness. Third, he said that the League of Nations is mired in the Lytton Report and ignores the 'current situation' of 'Manchukuo.' He also said, 'Japan cannot stand idly by and insists on peace in the East...'"

This kind of statement, except for Japan's own praise, all other responses are probably extremely discordant. After all, the violent acts of trampling on the territory of the Northeast, destroying peace in the East, tearing up all international conventions, and slaughtering our people, etc., are all actual manifestations of the Japanese army. The facts are obvious and cannot be concealed in any way. In the future, if its wild nature is unleashed, unless it is restrained with iron and blood, I am afraid it will never repent on its own, and its aggressive behavior will become more and more intense.

(3) Mediation Fails, Combat Begins

Japan does not recognize the mediation of the League of Nations, and insists on its aggressive claim of "recognizing the puppet." As the British Foreign Secretary said, "The League of Nations is not a supreme state and has no power to force member states to comply." Therefore, the League of Nations has no way to add sanctions to Japan's violence. Japan does not accept the advice of the League of Nations, so the mediation only declares failure. Moreover, Japan knows that the United States must currently cultivate its national power and dare not exaggerate war. Although Britain is not stable internally, it sometimes has to rely on Japan. The Soviet Union's energy is all focused on domestic construction, so how can it lightly provoke? Therefore, Japanese imperialism can rely on its military power to continue its policy of gradual encroachment, from Liaoning to Jilin and Heilongjiang to Yuguan. Now it vows to take Rehe. But what about us? Mediation has been declared a failure, and the Japanese army is gathering on the border. The "ultimatum" has arrived, and the combat is about to begin. In the future, war is unavoidable. To solve the Northeast issue and protect Rehe, it depends on how our country uses its own iron fist and how it pours out its own hot blood to reclaim the land and wash away the humiliation.

A Diplomatic Official Talks About the Past and Future of Sino-Japanese Relations 35

Diplomacy Gains Military Assistance and Wins a Moral Victory

Military Preparations Have Been Made for Rehe and Ultimate Victory Still Belongs to Us

(Nanjing) A diplomatic official talked with reporters on the 18th about the past and future of Sino-Japanese relations. Here is a summary: 1) During the dangerous period two or three months ago, the Anglo-American debt disputes were difficult to resolve, and the Nine-Power Treaty, the Washington Conference, etc., were all chaired by the United States. The League of Nations failed, and the United States found it difficult to stand idly by. Therefore, the British Foreign Secretary deliberately adopted a pro-Japanese stance to threaten the United States. It explicitly stated that Russia and the United States would not be invited to the conference, and it did not clearly oppose the puppet organization. The new compromise proposal by Drummond was also the same. If it were accepted by the League of Nations, then future diplomacy would be in a dead end. 2) The situation has changed, and there are several reasons for this. China's diplomacy has gained military assistance, and its attitude has remained firm. Since Ramsbotham came to China, he has repeatedly made serious recommendations to the government. The Anglo-American debt disputes have also gradually turned around, and the smaller countries have consistently upheld justice. The negotiation meeting is scheduled for March, and it can be implemented without the consent of the parties involved, so that Japan has no chance to create difficulties. 4) The territory that we have lost will still be recovered by us, which is a bright path. 5) The establishment of an autonomous government in the Eastern Provinces and the explicit statement that sovereignty belongs to all countries is also not regrettable. Anti-Opium Association Plans to Strictly Prohibit Drugs 37

(Nanjing) The Anti-Opium Association believes that the addiction to narcotic drugs is much easier than that of opium. In recent years, the popularity of drugs has exceeded the Yellow River and spread to the north and south of the Yangtze River. After investigating the situation in various places, people taking drugs such as red pills, golden pills, and white powder, and injecting morphine, in places such as Jincheng, Gaoping, Changzi, Changzhi, Mincheng, Qin County, Xiangyuan, Pingding, Shouyang, Yuci, Taigu, Qi County, Yangqu, and Taiyuan in Shanxi Province, Zhoucun, Weixian, Qingzhou, and Qingdao in Shandong Province, as well as southern Hebei, northern Henan, southern Anhui, Yixing and Wujin in Jiangsu, Jin, Qu, and Yan in Zhejiang, and Xiamen, Jinjiang, and Tong'an in Fujian, are the most prevalent areas. If it is not strictly prohibited, in a few years, it will be as widespread as opium throughout the country. Smoking opium can still prolong life, but those who take drugs will die in less than three to five years. For the sake of preserving the nation, only the local party and government organs can jointly take responsibility, urgently prevent it based on the actual situation, and prevent Chinese and foreign traitors from manufacturing and selling drugs in order to contain the source. Constantly warn the people anytime, anywhere not to take various drugs and inject morphine, and strive to make it known to every household. Those who violate the law, whether they manufacture, transport, or take drugs, will be severely punished according to the law once they are caught, and no leniency will be given. Four measures have been formulated for strict prohibition: 1) The local party and government organs shall formulate plans to prevent the spread of narcotic drugs based on the actual situation, submit them to the Director of the Civil Affairs Department, and strictly implement the aforementioned plans. The aforementioned plans shall be based on the principle of not conflicting with various laws and regulations, and special attention shall be paid to the manufacturing organs of drugs in order to eliminate the source of drugs. 2) The local party and government organs shall regularly make efforts to publicize the harm of drugs and the ban, and strictly make the people aware of the warning. The publicity period shall be held at least four times a year. 3) Establish drug rehabilitation centers. If people are caught taking drugs such as red pills, golden pills, and white powder, and injecting morphine, they shall be sent to the drug rehabilitation center and ordered to quit after being sent to the court for judgment. The aforementioned drug rehabilitation offenders shall be tested once every four months, and after the sixth test, if it is proved that they have not committed another crime, they shall be allowed to be exempted from the test. 4) The Regulations for the Management of Narcotic Drugs for Scientific and Medical Use shall be used to manage the quantity of drugs stored in pharmacies, hospitals, and other places, and the local governments shall be responsible for checking their sales and uses at any time. (18th dispatch)

Page 10

Deterioration of Franco-Italian Relations

Italy Ships Large Quantities of Military Supplies through Austria and Hungary. France Submits Strong Note to Austria. 76

Reuters, Rome, 17th – A batch of military equipment was recently transported from Italy through Austria for repairs. France, suspecting this was a secret supply to the Austrian Fascist Party, immediately submitted a strong note to the Austrian government. Britain has also joined in. According to a Paris correspondent for an Italian newspaper, the French note demands that the Austrian government return the military equipment to Italy or destroy it, and make a pledge regarding this matter to the British and French representatives. The Italians are very indignant about this, and there is fear that a conflict will arise between France and Italy because of this.

Havas, Paris, 18th – According to a report in an Italian newspaper, France seems to have sent a note to Austria regarding the smuggling of military equipment in Central Europe. The content of the note is no different from a true ultimatum. The Paris Morning Post reported that the Foreign Ministry believes the news reported by the Italian newspaper refers to the note sent to Austria jointly by France and Britain, and that it does not have the nature of an ultimatum.

Reuters, London, 18th – According to reliable sources, the French note to Austria is not an ultimatum, but presents a completely friendly nature. The British and French governments recently made friendly suggestions to Austria to resolve this matter. If negotiations fail, the matter will be handed over to the Council of the League of Nations for handling.

National News Agency, Paris, 17th – Fearing that the situation in the Balkans will cause another European war, France today sent an ultimatum-style note to Austria, demanding that Austria return to Italy within two weeks the large amount of military equipment that was transported from Italy through Austria to Hungary. It is said that the amount of military equipment is enough to supply a large army corps. According to the note's demands, the military equipment should be returned to the original sender, or it should be destroyed immediately. There are many other requirements, such as: (1) The Austrian government should provide France with guarantees proving that the military equipment has been destroyed or returned; (2) The Austrian government should thoroughly investigate whether any military equipment has leaked into Hungary through Austrian territory in the past; (3) Austria should complete the thorough investigation within two weeks and give France a guarantee. Since France issued this note, governments in various European countries have felt that the situation is quite serious. This fact is related to the recent Little Entente. Hungary, fearing oppression from the alliance of Romania, Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia, has had to take precautions against military aggression by neighboring countries. This may be the reason why Hungary purchased military equipment. Therefore, Romania and the other two members of the Little Entente strongly support France's issuance of this note. According to reports, France's move is the result of a month of detailed investigation and conflicting statements issued by Vienna. The Austrian government sent a reply to France, acknowledging that the military equipment was transported to the Hirtenberg factory, but said that it originally belonged to Austria and was now being transported for repairs. The Austrian government allowed it to be transported in because it could provide work for Austrian workers. An earlier Austrian reply acknowledged that the military equipment was transported to Hirtenberg, but said it was only in transit and was legal. France, however, considered the amount too large and refused to let the matter drop. According to the French Foreign Ministry, local officials in Hirtenberg declared that there were a total of 50,000 rifles and 200 machine guns. In addition, there were likely some airplanes, because they had seen airplanes fly over Austria into Hungary and had not returned. Later, the French government, due to the contradictory statements of the Austrian government and the alarmist remarks in socialist newspapers, became more determined to investigate the matter thoroughly. The socialists believe that it is better for these military supplies to fall into the hands of the Hungarians than other Balkan countries, because if Italy and Yugoslavia were to fall out, Hungary would be Yugoslavia's strongest neighbor.

National News Agency, Rome, 17th – At a time when the friendship between France and Italy is deteriorating, there is now a French protest regarding the Italian military equipment being transported from Austria to Hungary, and thus the international situation is becoming more serious. This French protest has been submitted to the Vienna government by the French ambassador. According to the Italian Popolo newspaper, this document is "the most vile article rarely seen in international relations." The Popolo also briefly described the process of the military equipment transportation case, saying that this is just a private transaction, and the so-called military equipment is just some old-fashioned rifles, which were seized from Austria by Italy during the European war. Now, because they are old, they are being sent back to the original manufacturer in Hirtenberg for repairs and modifications, so they can be resold. The Popolo further stated that the French protest letter took the form of an ultimatum and was a major insult to the independent state of Austria, because it completely disregarded international etiquette, and it is foreseeable that it will inevitably arouse resentment in other countries towards France, and condemn them as disruptors of peace.

Disarmament Conference French and German Delegates Engage in Heated Debate

Russian Representative Demands Amendment to British Proposal 77

Reuters, Geneva, 17th – Today, during the Disarmament Conference's discussion of France's proposal to set standards for the armies of European and other continental countries, shorten military service periods, and reduce the size of standing armies, the German and French representatives engaged in a heated debate on the conference floor. The French representative, Paul-Boncour, declared that the nature of the military equipment of certain countries, although legal, is quite capable of arousing militaristic ideas. The German representative, Nadolny, said that setting army standards is not a necessary condition for reducing armaments, and said that the current demands on Germany to reorganize its army must be considered carefully. Nadolny also refused to accept any blame from all parties regarding Germany.

TASS, Geneva, 17th – Today, at a meeting of the Political Committee of the Disarmament Conference, the Soviet Union's chief representative, Litvinov, proposed two amendments to the British disarmament proposal made a few days ago. According to the original British proposal, European countries would individually issue a declaration formally announcing the abolition of the use of any force to resolve international disputes. At the same time, all countries would issue a general declaration of disarmament agreement. At the time, Litvinov pointed out that the nature of the declaration proposed by Britain would only bind non-European countries to the Kellogg-Briand Pact, while European countries would be restricted from using force under any circumstances. Today, Litvinov proposed an amendment to remove the words limiting the declaration to European countries, making it universal. However, the declaration should simultaneously have a general declaration of disarmament agreement, and that declaration should also not be limited to temporary application. Litvinov explained his proposal by saying that the international announcement of the abolition of the use of all force and coercive acts should be stated in writing and jointly signed by all countries that have joined the Kellogg-Briand Pact, making it a formal international law. However, the Soviet Union's representative cannot agree to make different interpretations of aggression between European and non-European countries. If European countries are exceptionally guaranteed by this declaration, then non-European countries will suffer losses. In addition to the danger of being attacked by countries on the same continent, European countries are also likely to be attacked by countries on other continents. Finally, Litvinov stated that the British proposal to abolish the use of all force should be signed before the disarmament agreement is established. If it is believed that this declaration should be issued at the same time as the disarmament agreement, then it is unknown when that time will come, or that time may not come at all. Moreover, the governments of most countries are currently very short-lived. When the opportunity comes and various countries are ready to sign, a new government of one of the countries may appear and refuse to sign the declaration, which could overturn the established situation.

League of Nations Handles Colombian-Peruvian War 78

Reuters, Geneva, 18th – At a tense time when the League of Nations is dealing with the Sino-Japanese dispute according to Article 11 of the Covenant, the South American republic of Colombia has now also requested the League of Nations to invoke Article 15 of the Covenant. This action is the result of correspondence between the League of Nations and the parties involved. On February 16th, Peru sent a note to the League of Nations, referring to the situation in Tarapacá, saying that Peruvian troops are now defending their position to resist Colombian incursions. Last night, the chairman of the League of Nations Council Committee, Lester (representative of Southern Ireland), replied in a concise document, saying that Tarapacá is Colombian territory, and the committee does not understand why there is a Peruvian military position there, and asked for an explanation of this point as soon as possible. This morning, Colombia sent a long document to the League of Nations, requesting the rapid application of Article 15 of the Covenant. The Council has scheduled a special meeting on February 20th to deal with this matter.
