Third Floor: (28) Industrial Products Room, (29) Industrial Products Room, (30) Publications Room, (31) Sports Room. The venue is protected by soldiers from the 1st Company of the Municipal Security Team. In addition to the receptionists of the association, the venue and various exhibition rooms are maintained in order by male and female boy scouts from the Municipal Boy Scout Council.

Representatives from All Walks of Life Attended 102

Chu Minyi of the Executive Yuan, Wang Zhengting, Liu Yazi, and Mr. and Mrs. Cai Yuanpei of the Central Committee, Commercial Counselor Anlede of the United States, Wu Tiecheng, Mayor of Shanghai, Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Yang Xingfo, Vice President of the Central Research Institute, Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Chamber of Commerce, Dai Ji, Commander of the Garrison, Wen Hongen, Director of the Public Security Bureau, Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Education Bureau, Shen Yi, Director of the Public Works Bureau, Pei Huang, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, He Bingxian, Cai Wuji, Zou Bingwen, Xu Shanxiang, Yan Jiguang, Zhang Xianglin, Guo Weibai, Li Zechun, Xu Xinliu, Xu Baohua, and Ye Gongchuo, Liu Haisu, Wang Yansong, Wu Yun Chu, Qian Yongming, Zhao Jinqing, Chen Guangfu, Wang Boqi, Guo Shun, and other dignitaries from all walks of life, numbering more than 500 people, and more than 2,000 visitors.

Details of the Opening Ceremony 103

At 2 pm, the opening ceremony was held in the 6th Banquet Room on the ground floor. The portrait of the Prime Minister and the flags of the Party and the country were hung in the center of the stage, as well as a bird's-eye view of the Chinese Pavilion at the Chicago Exposition. Chairman Chen Gongbo presided over the ceremony, and Yang Bingxun took the minutes. First, the military band of the Public Security Bureau played music, followed by the most respectful salute to the flags of the Party and the country and the portrait of the Prime Minister. The Chairman solemnly read the Prime Minister's will and delivered the opening speech. He Bingxian, Chairman of the Standing Committee, reported on the preparations. Cai Wuji, Director of the Solicitation Department, reported on the solicitation process. Chu Minyi, representative of the Executive Yuan, delivered a speech. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, US Commercial Counselor Anle En, and Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce Wang Xiaolai delivered speeches in succession. Finally, music was played, photos were taken, and the meeting was adjourned. The preparatory committee then led the attendees on a tour.

Chairman's Opening Speech 104

Chairman Chen Gongbo delivered the opening speech, saying, "Today is the opening day of the Exhibition of Solicited Items for our country's participation in the Chicago Exposition. I am very happy to be able to gather with you all. Our country's participation in the Chicago Exposition began in February of the 19th year, when we received an invitation from the US government. In March of the 20th year, it was approved by the State Council. Due to internal and external troubles, the national crisis became more and more serious. It was not until June of last year that the preparatory committee was officially established and began to work. The estimated preparatory expenses were set at 400,000 yuan. This participation in the Chicago Exposition is of great significance for strengthening Sino-US friendship and developing foreign trade. At the inaugural meeting of the preparatory committee, Gongbo talked about the lessons learned from our country's previous participation in foreign expositions, and that this participation in the Chicago Exposition should use scientific methods to solicit exhibits, and that the government and the people should cooperate to ensure that all preparations are perfect. Since the preparations began last year, many provincial governments and industrial groups have enthusiastically participated in fundraising and soliciting exhibits. However, due to the difficult financial situation in some places, they have missed the opportunity to exhibit. This is something we deeply regret. However, given the current severe domestic situation and the financial difficulties of the central and local governments, we can be satisfied with the current achievements. The preparatory committee intends to create models or charts of the central government's construction plans and achievements in recent years, in addition to ordinary exhibits, to show the progress of our government's efforts to reform and govern after the reform. This exhibit has been contacted by the Ministry and various departments and agencies, and they are actively preparing it. Unfortunately, due to the limited time, they were unable to fully participate in the exhibition. I am very sorry to invite you to review it. Now I will report to you on Gongbo's thoughts on this preparatory exhibit."

Chairman Chen Gongbo Delivering the Opening Speech (Photo by Xu Tianzhang)

"The intention and hope of holding the exhibition of solicited items: (1) In addition to strengthening diplomatic relations, participating in foreign expositions is a good opportunity to promote domestic products and develop foreign trade. Most countries allocate huge sums of money from the government, and officials and civilians jointly prepare exhibits, so the organizers can prepare easily and achieve great results. Our government has financial difficulties and needs the enthusiastic participation and support of the industrial and commercial sectors in order to achieve good results. The preparatory committee has worked hard in this area for this solicitation, so it has been able to achieve today's results. It is hoped that the industrial and commercial sectors will continue to uphold this spirit of cooperation in the future, assist the government in every way, and various industries will have the hope of complete success. (2) In the past, when our country participated in foreign expositions, the exhibits were shipped back after the exhibition. Due to various reasons, some were damaged or lost, and the original items were not returned, so merchants regarded participating in expositions as a dead end. This solicitation has been quite difficult due to this influence, but the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has clearly promulgated the rules for soliciting exhibits, and the preparatory committee has repeatedly stated that it will be fully responsible for the exhibits, except for dangers that cannot be prevented by human power. This can be solemnly declared to the exhibitors. (3) This exhibit adheres to the principle of 'quality over quantity'. During the exhibition period, the preparatory committee will hire experts to conduct a rigorous review of all exhibits. It is hoped that all attendees and visitors will provide as much criticism as possible for reference during the review, and it is hoped that they will provide as much criticism and guidance as possible on the arrangement and display of the exhibits. (4) After this exhibition,"

"the qualified exhibits will be packed and shipped overseas. The preparatory committee and the representatives of the exhibitors who will accompany them to the United States are actively preparing for the future facilities and promotional materials and methods of the venue. It is hoped that the Chinese people will contribute their opinions in order to gather ideas and benefit widely. Although this solicitation for the competition cannot fully reflect the progress of the past century in the same way as other countries in the world, and the preparation is so rushed, Gongbo still hopes to win international praise on the shores of Lake Michigan, so as to learn from others' strengths and make up for our weaknesses, in order to promote the improvement of our industry and the promotion of domestic goods, and to change the situation of foreign trade surplus over the years."

Report on Preparation Progress 105

He Bingxian, Chairman of the Standing Committee of the Preparatory Committee, reported on the progress of the preparations, saying: The Preparatory Committee for the Republic of China's participation in the Chicago World's Fair was established on June 15th of last year, and it has been half a year now. During this half year, the Standing Committee of the Preparatory Committee has reported its work to the Preparatory Committee in writing once. That report was a vertical overview of the Standing Committee's activities, that is, the work of the Standing Committee in various aspects was listed separately. Now, due to time constraints, I cannot list them in such detail. I can only select a few important points to report to you. 1. The process of soliciting designs for the Chinese Government Pavilion. Regarding the solicitation of designs for the Chinese Government Pavilion, because we wanted to gather ideas from all sources, we published a solicitation notice in the newspaper. Later, the submitted designs were deemed unsuitable. Either the designs were too grand, which was not allowed by our budget, or they were too simple, and could not reflect the spirit of progress in our country's architecture over the past century. Therefore, the Preparatory Committee invited the Chinese Architects Association to design the pavilion. The Association generously agreed and volunteered to help the Preparatory Committee, for which the Preparatory Committee members are very grateful. The first design was approved by the Association and the Standing Committee. Later, we received a telegram from the Chicago World's Fair in the United States, saying that the area allocated to China had been changed. Because of this, the design was no longer suitable. The Architects Association, without complaint, designed a second design for us. The Standing Committee of the Preparatory Committee was very satisfied with this design and decided to adopt it. The design hanging here is this one. There is also a wooden model made according to this design, which is displayed on the first floor. After the meeting, please go and visit it. 2. Preparation situation for exhibits from various provinces. Director Cai will give a detailed report on the detailed situation of exhibits from various provinces later. Now I will briefly report on the organizations in various provinces responsible for collecting exhibits. The Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Hangzhou Municipal Government established a "Hangzhou to Participate in the Chicago World's Fair" organization. The Jiangxi Provincial Government established a "Jiangxi to Participate in the Chicago World's Fair" organization. In Guangzhou, a "Guangdong and Guangxi to Participate in the Chicago World's Fair Preparatory Office" was established. The remaining provinces, such as Hubei, Hunan, Anhui, Fujian, and Shaanxi, also established exhibit preparation offices. In the United States, there is also a "Preparatory Office for Chinese Painters Studying in the United States to Participate in the Chicago World's Fair." 3. Publicity plan. The Preparatory Publicity Department decided to focus on publicity in the United States. In order to make the world truly understand the actual situation of China's scientific and cultural progress over the past century, it is preparing to publish seven kinds of English pamphlets: 1. Our country's health undertakings; 2. The progress of Chinese science; 3. The progress of Chinese education; 4. Chinese agriculture; 5. Chinese industry; 6. Chinese silk; 7. Chinese tea. Each of these pamphlets contains about 40,000 words, and the Publicity Department has invited experts to write them. The purpose of these pamphlets is, on the negative side, to explain foreigners' misunderstandings about our country, and on the positive side, to enable them to understand our country's inherent culture and recent progress. 4. The task of sending a special envoy to the United States. Because the date of the Chicago World's Fair is very near, the Preparatory Committee has requested the Chairman to send someone to the United States to prepare everything. The Chairman has now appointed Guo Weibai, a member of the Preparatory Committee and Deputy Director of the Office, to go. His task is to supervise the construction of the Chinese Government Pavilion and negotiate the lease of land. Before the official appointment of the Chinese government representative, he will represent the Preparatory Committee to negotiate everything with the United States. 5. The purpose of the exhibit exhibition and the responsibilities of each committee member. The purpose of this exhibit exhibition is to publicly display various exhibits in the country before they are shipped to the United States, so that they can receive criticism and guidance from people from all walks of life. Originally, the Preparatory Committee also organized various review committees and invited experts to serve as reviewers. However, in order to gather ideas from all sources, we also ask you to visit and give your criticisms and guidance without reservation. Because these exhibits represent China's participation, in order to show China's progress over the past century and to make the world truly understand China, the Preparatory Committee members and the members of the review committee should certainly do their best to shoulder this responsibility. We hope that you will also take on this responsibility and generously give us all your criticisms and guidance.

Report on the Progress of Collecting Exhibits 106

Cai Wuji, Director of the Exhibit Department, reported on the progress of collecting exhibits, saying: Today is the opening of the Republic of China's Chicago World's Fair exhibit exhibition. I am very pleased to have officials and guests present. I was appointed Director of the Exhibit Department in June of last year, and I should give a brief report on all the circumstances of the exhibits to clarify the process. The most difficult aspects of collecting exhibits were: one was the items, and the other was the region. In terms of items, there are countless evolutionary items related to industry, agriculture, art, and science, such as Jiangxi's porcelain, Fujian's lacquerware, and silk, tea, and silk fabrics from other provinces. In terms of region, China is vast, and the provinces are far apart, and transportation is still not very convenient in many places. After repeated discussions, we decided that the purpose of collecting exhibits was to emphasize quality over quantity. On one hand, we asked the governments and organizations of various provinces and cities to assist in collecting exhibits. In August and September, we successively established exhibit sub-committees in Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Fujian, Guangdong and other provinces, which made the work more organized. Furthermore, it was difficult to motivate the exhibits from various regions if we did not personally contact them. Therefore, I and Miao Zhongxiu, the Deputy Director of the Exhibit Department, went to Zhejiang, Nanjing, Beiping, Tianjin, Yantai, Guangdong, Guangxi, Hong Kong, Xiamen, Shantou, Fujian and other places to contact them separately and promote them effectively. Now, the products from various provinces have been sent to the exhibition one after another, and they are so beautiful that one can't take it all in. Among them, the Nanjing's Nanjing silk brocade, Hangzhou's silk fabrics, Jiangxi's porcelain, and Beiping Jingxingzhai's jade lacquer carving tools, etc., have been successfully completed after a lot of time and effort. It is now estimated that there are more than 7,000 items, and although I dare not say that this is unprecedented compared to previous exhibitions, I feel that there has indeed been a lot of progress. China is a vast land with abundant resources, and if we can collect as much as possible, it should be more than this. Now, due to time and regional restrictions, omissions are unavoidable, and I must ask you to forgive me. The process of collecting exhibits is as described above. The Preparatory Committee originally intended to organize a review committee for the exhibits, and invited celebrities from all walks of life to review them. However, I thought that some of the exhibits collected this time might be advanced products in recent years, so it would be better to hold a public exhibition for all to visit. Therefore, we took this opportunity to review the exhibits and decided to hold an exhibit exhibition, and the Academia Sinica graciously lent us the new building here as the exhibition venue, which is something we are very grateful for. After we had a definite address, we moved the exhibit department, which was originally located on the Museum Road, to this place for office work in early January. As for the exhibition, it was originally scheduled to start on February 4, but the preparations started in mid-December of last year, and the procedures for displaying exhibits were extremely troublesome. In addition, the exhibits from afar had not yet been transported at that time, so we had to postpone the opening to today. Initially, we planned to open it very publicly without admission tickets, but because Shanghai is densely populated, if it were opened for free, it would inevitably be too crowded. In order to maintain order at the exhibition, we printed long-term tickets and ordinary tickets, and charged a small fee to limit the number of visitors. In summary, the exhibition will be open for only two full months from preparation to opening. The reason for the urgency is that the exhibits must be loaded onto ships at the end of February in order to arrive in time for the opening of the Chicago International Exposition on June 1. Although I know that this exhibition will inevitably be rushed due to time constraints, and the results of the exhibition may not be as good as expected, since I

Page 14

have undertaken the responsibility of preparation, I have always been devoted to my work, only advancing, never retreating. Therefore, during the two months of preparation, I supervised the staff, overcame all difficulties, and worked day and night. Even during the holidays, we all worked as usual. Today, we have managed to open the exhibition, but I still feel that the layout is not perfect, and it is inevitable that there will be some roughness and messiness. I must ask gentlemen from all walks of life to give as much guidance as possible, which is what I sincerely ask for. Because of the limited time today, I will only give this brief report. A detailed written report will be given in the future. Now, I will not go into details. In addition, I should also take this opportunity to express my gratitude to those who assisted in the collection and display of the exhibits, who gave us a lot of help.

Chu Minyi's Address 107

Chu Minyi, representative of the Executive Yuan, gave an address, saying: Today, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce is holding an exhibit exhibition in Shanghai in preparation for participating in the Chicago World's Fair. We must know that international exhibitions are held every few years. China participated in the Belgian exhibition in 1919. China did not participate in the Paris exhibition because it had colonial characteristics. China held the Nanyang Industrial Exposition 30 years ago. In recent years, China has participated in exhibitions in other countries more than once. However, the items we participate with are always porcelain, lacquerware, tea, silk, and so on. This year, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce specially set up an exhibit department to find ways to collect exhibits that can show the strengths of Chinese goods. Exhibitions have a great relationship with industry and commerce, and can enable Chinese goods to be sold abroad. In recent years, the foreign trade of our country's silk, tea, and other products has been severely hit. We must find ways to improve international trade. Participating in the exhibition is a new invention in the form of substantive improvements to commercial warfare methods.

Wu Tiecheng's Speech 108

Mayor Wu Tiecheng said in his speech: Today, the Republic of China's exhibit exhibition for participating in the Chicago World's Fair is being held in Shanghai, which is the most glorious event for Shanghai. After visiting various exhibits, we thought that in the process of continuous warfare and natural disasters in our country in recent years, the progress of industry has been so great, which is a comforting event. At the same time, we see the trend of Chinese industry, such as Fujian lacquerware and Jiangxi porcelain, which are very expensive and are only displayed as antiques, which are not needed by ordinary people. This shows that the progress of industry and manufacturing has not completely shaken off the old system. Therefore, people still prefer to buy foreign goods. Now, the first thing we must do is to promote industry, focusing on daily necessities. The porcelain kilns in Jingdezhen, Jiangxi, were originally used to supply the emperor, and if they continue to improve every day, it will not have a significant relationship with international fame. The second is to promote industry, which requires the government and the people to cooperate and find ways to improve commerce. The reason why industry cannot develop is that the organization of commercial institutions is incomplete. Commercial institutions should be responsible for promoting and improving how to sell industry. I hope that the government and the people will work together to promote industry. We believe that under such an effort, within a few years, China can open a large-scale exposition, and countries will also come to participate.

Speech by the American Consul 109

The American Commercial Consul An Laisi gave a speech in English, which was translated as follows: Today, on behalf of the American Department of Commerce, I am participating in the Republic of China's exhibit exhibition for participating in the Chicago World's Fair. Last year, I discussed the participation plan with the Minister of Industry and Commerce and the Exhibit Committee. The land allocated to China in Chicago is very important, close to the river.

It can attract the attention of visitors. At the same time, I hope that China can make full use of it. Sino-American friendship is valued by the general public. In the future, many people will visit the Chinese Pavilion, which can increase the friendly impression between the two countries. Now, when China is in a very difficult time, being able to take the exhibits to participate in the exhibition can represent the spirit of China and the progress of China. Therefore, on the one hand, it can arouse the concept of friendly people from both countries, and at the same time, it can increase commercial relations. On behalf of the American Department of Commerce, I express my full satisfaction with China's participation in the exhibition in the midst of all kinds of difficulties.

Display of Famous and Valuable Treasures 110

The products from various provinces and cities participating in the Chicago World's Fair have been transported to Shanghai, and the exhibit exhibition has been completed as of yesterday, with a total of more than 8,000 items, all of which are famous and unparalleled treasures. Among them, Chen Guozhi's sculptures and Hu Zupeng's Wangmu Shangshou Dragon Boat are the most valuable, worth US$10,000. There are countless other antiques. The most unique is the lacquerware from the Fujian Huier Orphanage, Sun Yat-sen, Yue Fei, Lin Zexu, Qi Jiguang, Lao Tzu, Wang Shouren, Confucius, Mozi, Biaozu, Guan Gong Guanyin, Huangdi, etc., each worth US$100.

Rules for Visiting the Exhibition 111

The exhibit exhibition will be held from yesterday to March 5. Long-term tickets are one yuan each, and ordinary tickets are 20 cents each. The exhibition hours are from 2:00 PM to 7:00 PM every day. The rules of the exhibition are as follows: 1. Visitors can only view the exhibits on display at the exhibition, and are not allowed to touch them. 2. Separate routes are designated for entering and exiting the exhibition hall, which are marked with road signs. 3. Visitors should walk in an orderly manner along the route to maintain order and avoid crowding. 4. Exhibitors may, due to the needs of the event, perform and explain the exhibits themselves or send someone to do so, but they must not hinder the visitors from visiting. 5. Visitors who are visiting the exhibition hall should not smoke cigarettes, make loud noises for no reason, or spit at will. 6. If visitors are drunk or behave abnormally, they may be persuaded to leave the venue by the staff of the exhibition. 7. If visitors have any questions or inquiries about the exhibits, they may ask the exhibition office. 8. Without the permission of the exhibition office, it is not allowed to take photos or sketches in the hall. 9. The staff and employees of the exhibition will wear badges to distinguish them. 10. These rules will be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Property Owners Association Petition Unsuccessful Amid Water Cutoffs

City Hall Closed, Residents to Petition Again on Monday/Residents Driven Away by Municipal Council While Demanding Water 112

Guowenshe reports the following on the water dispute:

Petition City Hall Again Next Monday 113

Shanghai Property Owners Association representatives Yan Yanfang, Shen Jixuan, Guo Zusheng, and eight others, based on the resolution of the members' meeting, went to the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday afternoon to petition, requesting negotiations with the Public Concession authorities to first open the water pipes for those who have had their water cut off, in order to save the lives of citizens, etc. Unexpectedly, yesterday was Saturday, and it was already the afternoon when it was the regular holiday. Mayor Wu and Secretary-General Yu were not in the City Hall. The representatives then went to the Chicago World's Fair Exhibit Preparatory Committee again to meet them, but both Wu and Yu were not there. So they rescheduled to petition the City Hall again at 10:00 AM on the 20th of the month (tomorrow).

Tense Situation/Water Cutoff with Force Continuing 114

As the water supply problem becomes more and more tense, the water company continues to cut off water with force. Yesterday afternoon around 2:00 PM, a foreign staff member of the company led five or six workers and more than a dozen armed police officers to Zhoujiapai Road, Yangshupu, to cut off the water in Shunchengli. There are 198 houses and more than 200 tenants in this neighborhood. For a time, the water source was cut off, and there was no way to appeal. After receiving the news, the landlord, Huada Company, immediately rushed to the Property Owners Association to report and ask for help.

Residents in Two Locations Demand Water from Municipal Council 115

Yesterday around 10:00 AM, residents of Weishuifang, Zhejiang Road, gathered 60-70 residents from the entire neighborhood, each carrying a lead bucket, and lined up to the Municipal Council Office at the corner of Hankou Road and Jiangxi Road to demand water because they had no water to drink. The General Patrol Room had received news in advance and dispatched a large number of Chinese and foreign patrol officers nearby in advance. When the residents arrived at their destination, a large team of patrol officers used batons to disperse the crowd, who went southeast. Not long after, more than 300 residents of Sanxingfang, Tangshan Road, Pudong, also each carried buckets and cans, and walked in formation from the northeast. When the patrol officers saw this, they again used batons to disperse them. Wang Yaozeng, Wu Wenyuan, and ten other representatives of the tenants of the neighborhood, entered the Municipal Council and asked Director-General Fessenden to answer. He De Kui, the director of the meeting, postponed the meeting. The representatives asked the Municipal Council to immediately order the water company to restore the water supply. He transferred the purpose of the representatives to state. Then, He came out and replied that Fessenden could go to the water company to contact him before this afternoon, and asked the representatives to come to the office next Monday to wait for a response. He did not get any results and left. Also, in order to maintain order in Sanxingfang, the Municipal Council has ordered the relevant police station to send two Chinese patrol officers to suppress it, so as to avoid accidents.

Opinions of Jiang Bingsheng, Standing Committee Member of the Property Owners Association 116

Jiang Bingsheng, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Property Owners Association, believes that the report of the American expert Mr. Hill is indeed fair, but the measures of the British Shanghai Water Company, although based on the report, are actually drawing a tiger and resembling a dog, and are even more intensified. Yesterday, he specially summarized Mr. Hill's report and added notes, and sent it to the Property Owners Association for reference. The following is a record: Mr. Hill said that the purpose of all public utilities is to supply goods at the lowest price, and the quality is suitable for the needs of users. Mr. Hill said that the public utility of water should pay more attention to safe and fixed supply than other public utilities. Where is the so-called safety and fixed supply when the company often cuts off water as a threat? Mr. Hill said that measuring the water sold with water meters is the only reasonable and fair way to open a water plant, because it can prevent unfairness and mutual discrimination for users. Mr. Hill said that installing water meters is the only effective way to limit household waste and is an economical way. The above-mentioned water meters refer to household installations, not total water meters. Mr. Hill said that the company's chief engineer once estimated that if all water meters were replaced, the daily consumption per person per household could be reduced from 33 gallons to 2 gallons. This also refers to household water meters. The so-called daily per person per household is the meaning of per household. Mr. Hill said that I believe that when discussing fair value and encountering exchange rate problems, to obtain a fixed water price standard, a fair average exchange rate must be used. If the income is calculated in silver, then the approved value should also be calculated in silver. "This is also obvious. "Mr. Hill said that in terms of the safety of investment, the certainty of income, and the market sales, the interest and income of Shanghai's main business are relatively high, especially when the company has to bear the exchange rate risk of its capital value. However, this danger has been discussed in this chapter and can be avoided by calculating capital in silver. "Also, the French Water and Electricity Company installs meters on a household basis, with no meter fee and no deposit. The Nanshi Water Company installs meters on a household basis, with no meter fee, and only collects a deposit. The Zhabei Water Company installs meters on a household basis, with no meter fee, and only collects a deposit. The British Shanghai Water Company has always charged users for installing water meters, and only collects a deposit, without any meter fee.

Municipal Council Information Office Asks for Correction 117

The Municipal Council Information Office sent a letter to this newspaper, saying: To the Editor of Shen Bao, On the 17th of this month, your newspaper published a report on the water cutoff incident in Sanxingfang, Tangshan Road, which stated that residents elected representatives, went to this Bureau, and were personally received by Director-General Zhong Sijun, who also had a conversation, saying that the water meter installation was decided by the Municipal Council, and that the company cut off the water because the water fee had not been collected, which was not against the law. After investigation, Zhong Sijun did not meet with these representatives on that day, nor did he make such a statement. I am sending this letter to you for correction. Yours sincerely, The Editing Department of Shen Bao, 18th.

Temporarily Sets Donation Goal at 200,000 Yuan, Yu Qiaqing Recommended as Chairman 118

| Changzhou Association Follows Suit |

The Ningbo Shanghai Association held a joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members yesterday to raise funds to purchase a Ningbo Shanghai aircraft. Li Zongtong Talks About the First Batch of Antiquities Moved South

Siku Quanshu is Complete and Intact/Scattered Word Plate is from the Shang and Zhou Dynasties/Kuai Xue Shi Qing is the Most Precious 119

Central News Agency reports: The first batch of 2,118 boxes of antiquities from the Palace Museum that were moved south have long been transported to Pukou. The storage location was originally designated as No. 26, Rue de l'Eglise, French Concession, Shanghai, but the Central Political Conference decided to move them to Bianluo for storage. However, yesterday's Beijing news said that Bianluo does not have a suitable storage location and will still be transported to Shanghai. In order to clarify the truth, the Central News Agency reporter specially visited Li Zongtong, Secretary-General of the Palace Museum, who had just arrived in Shanghai from Beiping, yesterday morning. He answered as follows:

Address Still Undecided 120

There are three places in Beiping that store antiquities: the Palace Museum, the Antiquities Exhibition Hall, and the Peking University Library. The Exhibition Hall and Peking University have had fires, and some of the calligraphy and paintings are missing. The antiquities moved south this time are from the Palace Museum. The first batch has a total of 2,118 boxes. The previous rumor that three boxes were damaged is completely untrue. The first batch originally scheduled to be moved south was 2,121 boxes, but three of the calligraphy and painting boxes were extremely long and could not fit in the carriages, so they were temporarily suspended. The rumor that they were damaged due to careless handling is not aware of the care taken during handling. The box items are numbered and the names of the handlers are registered for responsibility. The assembly of the box items is very strong and would not be damaged even if they fell to the ground. This batch of antiquities has arrived in Pukou. After the Central Political Conference decided to move them to Bianluo, a telegram was sent to Bianluo to find a storage location. Now it is known that it is difficult to find a suitable location in Bianluo for the time being, so there is a proposal to transport them to Beijing for storage, but it has not been determined yet.

First Batch of Valuables 121

Among the first batch of antiques, there are over six hundred boxes of the "Siku Quanshu" (Complete Library of the Four Treasuries), red books, and historical records.

These account for one train car. The rest are jade artifacts, bronzes, porcelain, carvings, calligraphy, and paintings, etc. There were originally seven copies of the "Siku Quanshu" in the country, but only three remain. The one remaining in Beiping is the Wen Yuan Ge copy, the one in Jehol is the Wen Wei Ge copy, and the one in Shenyang was looted by the Japanese army during their invasion of Shenyang. The remaining copy is the Wen Su Ge copy. The Wen Lan Ge copy in Hangzhou is incomplete. The copy being transported south this time is the one stored in the Wen Yuan Ge in Beiping, which is the most meticulously edited and accurate. The red books are the complete set of imperial edicts from the Kangxi and Qianlong Emperors of the former Qing dynasty. The historical records are summaries of Qing dynasty memorials, all of which are extremely valuable items. Among the calligraphy and paintings, Wang Xizhi's "Kuaixue Shiqing" (Timely Clearing After a Quick Snowfall) is the most precious, as Wang Xizhi's original works are already rare. This piece is also one of the "Three Rarities." It was recently rumored in Beiping that there was a calligraphic couplet by Wang Xizhi, but that is not accurate. Among the bronzes, the "San Zi Pan" (Three-Character Basin) dates from the Shang and Zhou dynasties. The basin has many characters inscribed on it, sufficient for archaeological research. Among the porcelain, "Guyuexuan" porcelain is the most famous and valuable, all of which dates from the early Qing dynasty. There is also a bronze figure, in a half-kneeling position, holding a piece of white paper, which can write the eight characters "Ba Fang Xiang Hua, Jiu Tu Lai Wang" (Eight Directions Turn Towards Civilization, Nine Lands Come to Pay Homage). It was a gift from England during the Qianlong Emperor's celebratory birthday. In addition, there are large self-ringing clocks, which play music when they strike the hour, and large jade mountain dog mirrors, etc., which could not be moved due to their extraordinary bulkiness. Mr. Li also said that when they were moved south, the president of the Song dynasty academy telegraphed to the local people in Beiping, expressing that the southward movement of the antiques was to protect the lifeblood of Chinese culture and had no other meaning. As soon as the situation stabilizes slightly, they will be moved back to their original locations for preservation.

Sudden Increase in Shipments from the Yangtze River

Fear of Japanese Military Blocking Sea Ports 122

Recently, the situation in North China has become tense. Japanese warships on the Yangtze River have been increasing in number since the 15th. In addition, newspapers are reporting that the Japanese military will blockade our ports after hostilities break out. After this news spread, Yangtze River merchant guilds have been telegraphing Shanghai frequently, urging the early transport of goods that have already been purchased. Therefore, since the 17th, export goods on the Yangtze River ships of the six companies in this port have suddenly become congested, increasing by one or two times compared to the previous few days. This is because they deeply fear that transportation will be cut off after the war, and therefore merchants are expediting the shipment of goods in advance.

Japan's Trade with China in January

Exports and Imports Both Increased Compared to the Same Period Last Year 123

The Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office in this port received an official telegram from Tokyo yesterday, reporting on trade with China in January. The total value of Japan's exports to China this month was 9 million yen, while the result was an import surplus of 1.7 million yen. Compared to the same period last year, exports increased by 80%, imports increased by 38%, and the import surplus decreased by 34%. Breaking it down by region, exports to North China increased by 30% compared to the same period last year, imports increased by 5%, exports to Central China increased by 21%, imports increased by 94%, exports to South China increased by 34%, imports increased by 60%, imports from Hong Kong increased by 20%, and trade with the three northeastern provinces saw exports totaling 15 million yen, resulting in an import surplus of 2 million yen. Compared to the same period last year, exports increased by 135%, imports increased by 27%, and the import surplus decreased by 65%.

Draft Budget of the Public Works Department of the Municipal Council 130

The budget of the Public Works Department of the Municipal Council for this year has been reviewed by the Public Works Committee and submitted to the Board of Directors on Wednesday of this week. All items that have been approved will be listed in the draft general budget, pending further review by the Finance Committee.

Regular Expenditure Under the heading of regular expenditure, excluding education expenses, the total amount of expenditure after several reductions is 4,287,490 taels. This figure is approximately 72,000 taels more than last year. The initial estimate in November of last year exceeded the number by more than 210,000 taels.) Items reduced include one water truck by 18,000 taels, one road roller by 8,000 taels, lawn mowers reduced to 600 taels, typewriters reduced to 1,300 taels, file cabinets reduced to 2,000 taels, furniture and sundries reduced to 8,000 taels. In addition, the cost of automobile transportation has increased compared to the past. This is because the cars used by the bureau are of different styles, the work is tighter, and the drivers need two shifts, so the expenditure is relatively large. However, the Public Works Department is constantly paying attention to savings. In addition, there is 120,000 taels under the item of garbage transportation fees, which is a donation indirectly paid to the Municipal Government.

Temporary Expenditure Under the heading of temporary expenditure, according to convention, those that the Board of Directors has already approved or considered urgent are marked with the letter "A," and those that are deemed unnecessary to spend this year due to financial or other reasons are marked with the letter "C." After joint consideration by the Finance Department and the Public Works Department, the temporary needs of each department this year, excluding the repayment of public bonds and the allocation of necessary funds, total approximately 8 million taels. If this is done, it will also require adding a burden of approximately 500,000 taels in the coming year, because this includes the medical improvement fee and the educational construction fee plan. The acting director of the Finance Department believes that when preparing the budget, the amounts proposed by each department must be effectively reduced. The following items have all been considered:

Bridge Construction Fee The construction of a new bridge on Suzhou Creek on Jiangxi Road was originally planned to allocate 50,000 taels this year. The Director of Public Works believes that it can be delayed, so it has been marked with the letter "C." The tail end of the Tang En Road Bridge costs 920 taels, marked with the letter "A." The cement bridge on the Kulun Road Sha Jing Port is listed at 15,000 taels, and the cement bridge on the Jiaxing Road Hongkou Creek is listed at 20,000 taels, both marked with the letter "A." The cost of repairing riverbanks in various places is 20,000 taels, also marked with the letter "A."

Ditch and Canal Fee All drainage ditch fees, except for those on Qiqihar Road, Pingliang Road, and Meizhou Road, which are listed with the letter "C," are marked with the letter "A." The Director of Public Works believes that this work is already lagging behind. For the sake of developing and maintaining roads, this repair ditch fee cannot be delayed. In addition, the cost of repairing sewage ditches is 295,000 taels, listed with the letter "A." Building a pumping station on Putuo Road costs 20,000 taels, listed with the letter "C." Installing a manure loading station costs 5,000 taels, listed with the letter "A." In addition, the pumping equipment in various places costs a total of 46,000 taels, reduced by 2,500 taels, also listed with the letter "A."

Wharf Fee The remaining funds for the Qiwupu Road wharf are listed at 145,000 taels. Because part has already been spent, it has been changed to 115,000 taels, listed with the letter "A." The remaining amount for the Zhaofeng Road wharf is 10,000 taels, listed with the letter "A."

Park Fee The remaining amount for purchasing land for the Singapore Road Park is 175,000 taels, listed with the letter "A." In accordance with the previous discussion, a model boat pool is listed for Zhaofeng Park, costing 20,000 taels. After discussion, it was listed with the letter "C." Paving grass and building slopes on the protruding area of Hongkou Park near the shooting range to create a ball field costs 3,000 taels. After discussion, it was marked with the letter "A." In addition, the two parks on Jiaozhou Road and Poyang Road also have slight expansion costs.

Construction Fee Expanding the greenhouse in Zhaofeng Park costs 3,000 taels, listed with the letter "A." In addition, building fences for the visitor tea and snack area costs 7,500 taels, also listed with the letter "A." The cost of adding equipment to the two incinerator plants is 43,000 taels, listed with the letter "A." A storage room and office in Xinzha costs 18,000 taels. The tail end of the Xinzha freight car room costs 15,000 taels, and the Tongzhou freight car room costs 35,000 taels. All three items are listed with the letter "A." If possible, the Public Works Department will still reduce them. In addition, a cement cargo shed in Xinzha costs 12,000 taels, adding toilets in various places costs 15,000 taels, and public drinking pools cost 3,000 taels, all of which are also listed with the letter "A."

Road Fee The extension and widening of roads and the purchase of land, etc., were originally listed at 1.8 million taels. Based on last year's experience and the Board of Directors' policy of gradual progress in collecting local taxes, the Director of Public Works proposed that this item be changed to 1.4 million taels, which is listed with the letter "A." In addition, the road repair fee was originally listed at 392,800 taels. The Director of Public Works stated that last year 350,000 taels were listed, which was already overspent. It is difficult to estimate the amount of this expenditure within a year's range, but the Public Works Department's road repair plan in recent years is insufficient to meet the public's needs, especially in the eastern district. Therefore, even if we proceed cautiously, we are still afraid that this number will be insufficient. The number was then revised to 400,000 taels, listed with the letter "A."

Record of Joint Meeting of North and South Market Rice Merchants 131

Yesterday, the North and South Market rice merchants held a joint meeting at the Cuixiu Hall of the Bean and Rice Industry Association. More than 100 people attended. Zhu Zixiang was elected as chairman. After the meeting was opened, it was reported that the industry had reduced the commission paid to customers by two tenths of the original commission. However, the rebates to store owners have not only not been reduced, but have even exceeded the regulations, which is regrettable. Now that we have received letters from colleagues requesting the rectification of commissions, it should be filed for discussion. It was decided that the current rebate is six tenths, with accounts cleared at the end of the month, and the rebate is three tenths, with accounts not cleared at the end of the month, and there will be no rebate at all to prevent sabotage. For the sake of the resolution, a small group will be established to supervise each other to ensure compliance. 2) After the industry used the city dipper, due to thrift and consumption, the authorities allowed the use of six-dipper city dippers. However, outsiders did not understand the truth and pointed out that it was a discarding of government orders. However, the simultaneous use of five-dipper and six-dipper dippers does not result in any loss for either the industry or customers. It should be discussed whether it hinders the new system of unified weights and measures. It was decided that the new measuring instruments should be promoted in accordance with the One Two Five decree and the five-dipper city dipper should be used. It was decided that starting from the 21st, the five-dipper city dipper will be approved for use, and all six-dipper city dippers will be discarded to comply with government orders.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Asks the Municipal Council to Strictly Arrest Bandits 136

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Shanghai International Settlement Municipal Council yesterday, requesting strict arrest of bandits in the settlement. The original letter stated, "We are writing to you to inform you that on the morning of the 17th of this month, the Shanghai Clock and Watch Industry Association sent a letter stating that, according to reports from members such as Meihuali, Hengdali, Yitaixiang, Zhongmei, Shi Weiji, Hengdeli, Maodeli, Huade on Nanjing Road, and Yicheng, Nanchang, Yuanyuan, Yuchang, Lehua, and Samsung on Fuzhou Road, the Shanghai Settlement is a district where commercial gatherings from around the country, and it is also a den where bandits are hiding. In recent years, bandits have specialized in robbing clock and watch shops. The patrol police have not yet solved the cases. The time of the robbery is usually between 5:00 PM and 9:00 PM. For example, the Nanchang Clock and Watch Shop on Fuzhou Road was robbed on February 2nd, losing watches worth more than 1,000 yuan. That incident occurred at around 6:30 PM. Although the bandits take advantage of this twilight opportunity when the lights are not yet on, it is also due to the patrol police's lack of thorough protection. Moreover, the patrol police rarely solve cases of theft from Chinese merchants. We Chinese people bear the obligation of paying taxes, and it does not seem appropriate to treat us with prejudice. We should ask your council to correct this." According to this, the 38th Executive Committee meeting discussed and decided that the repeated theft cases in the settlement are due to the patrol police's negligence, and the Chamber should send letters to the Chinese Ratepayers Association and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, transferring the matter to the Municipal Council for negotiation. The patrol police should be strictly ordered to increase the number of patrol police patrolling Nanjing and Fuzhou Roads every day from 5:00 PM to 9:00 PM, and supervise and urge the patrol police to arrest the criminals in the theft cases that have occurred as soon as possible, in order to eliminate the harm in the bud. These words are recorded in the minutes. In addition to sending letters to the Chinese Ratepayers Association, we have always looked up to your council as a model for the Chamber of Commerce to rescue and respond to emergencies. We are sending this letter to request you to investigate and promptly transfer the matter to the Municipal Council for handling, to fulfill our public duty. It is a matter of public interest to you. The fact that Fuzhou Road is a prosperous location in the settlement, and the time between 6:00 PM and 7:00 PM is the peak of commercial activity, the theft that occurred at Nanchang Clock and Watch Shop this time. If the patrol police had been adequately prepared beforehand, the bandits would not have dared to be so bold and reckless. After the robbery, they were able to remain at large. Your bureau should be responsible for the protection of Chinese and foreign merchants in the settlement. The accident caused by the patrol police's negligence should be given special attention. We must solve the case and recover the stolen goods as soon as possible. In accordance with the information in the letter, we hereby write to your bureau to request you to investigate and handle the matter accordingly. To the Public Concession Bureau of Public Works, this is addressed.

Memorial Site Located in Zhabei 137

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng and more than 50 prominent figures from all walks of life initiated the construction of a memorial monument and public cemetery for police officers killed in the line of duty. Summary of Labor Dispute Resolutions 138

Shao Wansheng The labor dispute over the dismissal of employees at the Shao Wansheng dried goods store on Nanjing Road was resolved yesterday when the store's manager, Shen Songgao, in order to avoid prolonging the dispute, invited Yu Yaoqiu, a representative of the dried goods workers' union, to discuss a resolution. As a result, the company provided subsidies to the dismissed employees as severance pay. The union representative immediately returned to the union to report the situation to the store's employees. The employees were also willing to settle the matter peacefully and expressed their acceptance. The union representative, Yu Yaoqiu, then collected the full amount of the severance pay, declared the resolution, and reported it to the party and government organs to close the case.

Dasheng Cotton Weaving Factory The Dasheng Cloth Factory on Zhongxing Road in Zhabei announced its closure this month and dismissed all 69 male and female workers, filing a case with the party and government organs. On the workers' side, they requested assistance from the Sixth District Cotton Weaving Industry Union. As a result of mediation by the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau, both parties signed a five-item resolution as follows: 1) The Dasheng Hongji Cloth Factory is allowed to close down. 2) All 69 workers in the factory are allowed to be dismissed. The company will provide severance pay separately, in the following amounts: (A) Those who have worked for less than three months will be given five days' wages. (B) Those who have worked for more than three months but less than one year will be given ten days' wages. (C) Those who have worked for more than one year but less than three years will be given twenty days' wages. 3) Daily wages will be calculated at 40 cents per ocean for the cloth machine department and 30 cents per ocean for the yarn-spinning department. 4) Item 2 of the reconciliation agreement reached between labor and management on December 31 last year, which stipulates that the factory should pay subsidies to the 11 employees who are working, must be supplemented in full as before. 5) If the factory is still restored to business by the old shareholders in the future, the old workers must be hired first.

Wang Fuji Foundry Wang Fuqi Foundry, located at the Li Family Residence on Luban Road in Nanshi, recently had a dispute due to the owner, Pu Ziqing, dismissing more than 30 workers, including Lu Bingquan and Zhou Binglin. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau specially convened both labor and management at 2:00 PM the day before yesterday to mediate. As a result, a four-item resolution was signed as follows: 1) The four workers who voluntarily resigned, Lu Bingquan, Zhou Binglin, Yang Rurong, and Bi Rongsheng, will each be given a month's wage as a subsidy. 2) The remaining workers will all be reinstated. 3) The factory will provide food during the shutdown period. 4) The severance pay for the resigned workers will be collected from the bureau on the 19th of this month.

Change of Method for the Rising Water Ball at the Pao Taiwan

Change of High Water Ball to High Water Board and Proposed Addition of Storm Warning Red Light 139

In the past, the Jianghai Customs River Conservancy established several flat houses (commonly known as flag-raising rooms) at the Wusong Fort, Taiwan Pu Wharf. They appointed Pang Baolin, Song Yinlang, and others familiar with navigation to be stationed there, specifically to manage and protect the safety of shipping lanes and ensure the smooth passage of ships. Next to the houses, there were massive lighthouses and tall masts, each. At the top of the lighthouses, large lights shone in four colors—green, yellow, black, and red—according to the cardinal directions, the light beams reaching far to serve as beacons for incoming ships. On the masts, large black (circular bamboo) balls were hoisted, called high-water balls. As the Sanjia Estuary is a crucial thoroughfare for ships of all nations entering and leaving Shanghai, daily and nightly shifts were assigned to officials to watch over it. The height of the tide was indicated by the hoisting of the balls at any time, and lights were displayed at night to report the water level to prevent obstructions. A "half-foot ball" was typically used; for example, if the level was 30 feet 5 inches, the "30 and a half-foot" ball was raised. If the level rose another five inches, the "31-foot" ball would be raised. Now, the Shipping Bureau has newly established regulations, planning to abolish the half-foot ball to avoid confusion. It is also heard that the current round balls will be replaced with square balls, with each square ball representing five feet. Two square balls hung together would indicate a rise of ten feet. The high-water balls will be replaced by high-water boards, pointed at the top and flat at the bottom. When the tide rises, the pointed end will face upwards; when the tide recedes, the pointed end will face downwards. At night, a green light and a white light will each be hoisted: when the tide rises, the green light will be above and the white light below; when the tide recedes, the white light will be above and the green light below. Furthermore, it is planned to add a red light to warn of storms to prevent navigational dangers. These newly established regulations have not yet been promulgated.

Preparations by the Benevolent Childcare Association to Aid Children in the North China War Zone

Deputy Director Chen Tiesheng Goes North for Inspection 140

The situation in Northeast China grows more perilous by the day. Under the sneering face of war, countless of our compatriots are sacrificing themselves on the battlefields. The China Benevolent Childcare Association, in preparation for aiding children in the North China war zone, has specially dispatched Deputy Director Chen Tiesheng, who departed from Shanghai this morning to inspect areas in Beiping, Tianjin, Rehe, and Luanxian. Murder Case Solved

Cause of Death of Ms. Lu Mao Established, Wang Jinyun Arrested the Night Before 141

Lu Mao, a housewife who ran a barber shop at No. 219 Yaoshui Lane, Xiaoshadu, West Shanghai, was suddenly confronted on January 26th at about 5:20 AM by two thugs speaking with a Northern accent and wearing long blue cloth robes. The thugs dragged her out and shot her in a premeditated act of revenge, hitting vital organs, and she died almost instantly. It has now been learned that the truth behind the shooting is that there were three or four thugs, all residing in Meifang Li on Roberts Road, West Shanghai. They had learned that Lu, the barber shop owner, had some savings and had coveted it for a long time, but lacked an opportunity. As it was approaching the end of the lunar year, they went to Lu to extort 200 silver dollars under false pretenses. They were menacing, coaxing and compelling, and pestered him several times without success. The shop owner Lu, fearing their continued harassment, temporarily hid elsewhere. On that morning, just before dawn, the thugs assumed that Lu would be at home and went with their guns. To their surprise, they stormed into the shop but could not find Lu anywhere. Enraged, they dragged out the housewife, Lu Mao. Realizing the danger, she loudly called for help. Knowing that their plan had failed, the thugs shot her to vent their anger, and then fled. After receiving a report, Gu Wentao, a patrol officer from the 6th Precinct of Roberts Road, took charge of the investigation due to the seriousness of the case. He received information that one of the perpetrators, Wang Jinyun, was hiding with his concubine in No. 808 Changan Road, Zhabei. Officer Gu, along with Detective Team Leader Xia Pinshan, Deputy Team Leader Tang Bingsheng, and Detective Cao Chuqiao, secretly went to the address the night before. They arrested Wang Jinyun (from Henan) and his concubine Wang Zhao on the spot and took them back to the station for temporary detention, pending further investigation and pursuit of the other accomplices.

Tram Crushes Liu Yongyuan in Tragic Accident

Body Examined Yesterday Morning 142

Liu Yongyuan, age 21, from Suzhou, resided at No. 16, Huaxing Road, Zhabei. His father, Liu Fengchang, worked in a clothing store. At around 8 PM on the 16th of this month, Yongyuan was at Nanjing Xiangfen Lane, intending to cross the road from north to south. At that moment, it suddenly started raining heavily, and the road became very slippery. As he stepped onto the tram tracks, he slipped and fell. At that moment, Tram No. 34, with the character 皮, was traveling west. The driver, Cui Wenjin, saw Liu but could not brake in time and ran him over, causing severe injuries. His intestines spilled out, and blood flowed like a fountain, a gruesome sight. The patrolmen who arrived at the scene immediately reported the incident to the Zhabei Police Station. The police ordered an ambulance to take him to Renji Hospital, but he died shortly after. The body was taken to the forensic examination office on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court commissioned Prosecutor Guo Wei to conduct an autopsy. Cui Wenjin testified that he had been driving trams for three years and was not driving fast at the time and that he had rung the bell. He added that he saw the deceased fall on the tracks, so it was too late to stop, resulting in the accident. A witness, Austrian national Pirigripi, testified that on that day, he was sitting in the tram and saw a Chinese person covering their face and walking across the road about five yards away from the car. But that he did not see whether he was hit by the car or slipped. According to the statement of the deceased's father, Liu Feng, Mr. Guo determined that Liu Yongyuan died from abdominal injuries sustained after being hit by Tram No. 34. The body was released to his father, Liu Fengchang, for burial.

The Hai Su Series to be Published Successively 144

To popularize art among the masses, the China Book Company specially invited Mr. Liu Haisu, a leading figure in China's emerging art scene, to compile the "Hai Su Series" in the seventeenth year [of the Republic, i.e. 1928]. It contains masterpieces by famous artists from various countries and eras, as well as representative works by Mr. Liu himself, with systematic commentary. Mr. Liu extensively collected materials and painstakingly wrote, spending two years to complete the manuscript. The series consists of three parts, totaling six volumes and 300,000 words, with 700 illustrations. The first part is the Western Painting Collection, the second part is the National Painting Collection, and the third part is Haisu's National Paintings and Haisu's Western Paintings. The printing process took three years, and any slight blurring would be deleted by Mr. Liu and re-engraved, making it exquisite and unparalleled in the country. The Western Painting Collection has been widely sold since its publication last year, especially to art galleries, which have praised it highly. Newspapers have also repeatedly praised it, making it an immortal masterpiece in China's art world. The Western Painting Collection is divided into two volumes, focusing on modern art and tracing the general source and flow of modern art. Therefore, it starts with the Renaissance, the general source of modern art, and continues to the 20th century. The table of contents for the first volume includes: (1) The Phenomenon and Trends of the Rapid Development of Modern Painting, (2) Painting of the Early Renaissance, (3) Great Talents of the Renaissance, (4) Various French Painting Schools After the Renaissance, (5) Constable, (6) Corot. The table of contents for the second volume includes: (1) Impressionist Painting, (2) Post-Impressionism, further divided into (1) Introduction, (2) David – Pioneer of Post-Impressionism, (3) Cézanne – Father of Emerging Art, (4) The Life of Cézanne, (5) Van Gogh – Mad Genius, (6) Gauguin – Creator of Primitive Style, (7) Gauguin and Cézanne, (8) Matisse – Fierce General of Fauvism, (9) Cubism, (10) Expressionism, (11) Futurism, (12) Vries, etc. Mr. Liu uses a lively and vivid style to describe the artistic trends of various eras and the lives and works of the great masters, paying more attention to interesting anecdotes, which is different from the nature of general art history. Chinese art scholars lack both art museums for observation and accurate reproductions. The book's illustrations and text complement each other, with particularly rich publications on modern masterpieces, allowing general scholars to pursue the path of true art and increasing the appreciation of art lovers. The full set is priced at 20 yuan, with a special price of 15 yuan. For the purpose of popularizing purchases, a further 10% discount will be offered until February. Art lovers and art collectors should seize this opportunity to purchase a copy. It is heard that the second part, the National Painting Collection, and the third part, Haisu's National Paintings and Western Paintings, will also be published successively soon.

The Ferocity of Police Officer Li Zhang: First Killing the Patrol Chief and His Wife, Then Committing Suicide

Li Zhang Used Opium, Secretly Reported by Patrol Chief, Causing Li to Fear Punishment and Commit This Heinous Act 146

Li Zhang, a 38-year-old police officer from Hefei at the Hongqiao Town Police Station of the Sixth District, First Precinct of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, was addicted to opium. Circumstances of the Sinking of the Jinshunxing Sailing Ship

All Eight Crew Members Rescued, Cargo and Ship Sunk in the River, Responsibility for the Accident to be Determined Today 147

The large sailboat Jinshunxing of the Wusong Penglai Sailing Ship Guild collided with the Guangxiang Steamer near Baoshan on the 16th and sank. The sailors were rescued, but the cargo and ship were lost. The Maritime Affairs Bureau is investigating the incident today. The details are as follows:

Report to the Harbor Master: The Dada Steamship Company yesterday reported to the Jianghai Customs Harbor Master, stating that according to a report from Fang Xinli, the owner of the Guangxiang, the ship sailed from Tongzhou to Shanghai on the 16th of this month at 4:30 AM. At 10:48 AM, the ship passed the Lianghe Tunnel. The ship was traveling southeast with the current. At 11:15 AM, they saw a sailboat (the Jinshunxing) ahead, bearing about 12 degrees to the ship's starboard side, heading straight northwest. If the sailboat had not changed direction and continued on that course, a collision would not have occurred. However, two minutes later, they saw the sailboat suddenly turn north and move sideways. The ship sounded two blasts of the horn as a warning, but the sailboat ignored it. To prevent danger, the ship sounded the horn again and steered east to give way. However, the sailboat sailed sideways with full sails, intending to pass in front of the ship, but instead collided with the ship's starboard side, breaking two holes in the iron plate of the front hatch. The sailboat's bow was damaged, and it began to take on water and sink. The ship stopped to provide assistance, and the eight crew members of the sailboat lowered a sampan, unloaded their luggage, and boarded the ship for about ten minutes before the sailboat sank. The ship brought the sampan and the eight crew members to Shanghai. They arrived at the port at 2 PM. This is the truth of the sailboat colliding with the ship. The report to the Maritime Affairs Bureau is the same.

Lost Cargo: Yao Shunlai, the owner of the Jinshunxing, was also brought to Shanghai by the Guangxiang. He stated that all eight crew members were unharmed and did not fall into the water. They immediately boarded the sampan, so there were no injuries. The sailboat was carrying 1,280 bags of crude salt, each weighing over 50 catties, from Daishan to be unloaded in Liuhe. The Jinshunxing was a large two-sail sailboat. After the collision, it sank, and all the cargo was lost, but the crew members and their personal belongings were retrieved. There were no drownings or falls into the water. Yesterday, Yao Shunlai and the crew members returned to Wusong to report to the Sailing Ship Guild.

Ship Inspection Today: After receiving the report, Director Zhu of the Maritime Affairs Bureau initially planned to send technicians for inspection yesterday. However, due to the Guangxiang's schedule, it sailed to Tongzhou and is expected to return to Shanghai today. The Maritime Affairs Bureau has rescheduled the inspection to take place at noon today. Yang Qijue was specially dispatched to Shanghai by the Wusong Penglai Sailing Ship Guild yesterday to negotiate with the Dada Company. The Dada Company explained the cause of the accident, proving that the Jinshunxing sailed sideways and collided with the Guangxiang, causing it to sink. Therefore, the fault lies with the sailboat. Upon hearing this, Yang had no choice but to wait for the Maritime Affairs Bureau's investigation to determine the responsibility.

Chinese Sailing Ship "New Horizon" Sets Sail Today

Expected to Reach New York, USA in Seven Months, Resting Briefly Before Returning East Via Europe and Africa 148

American John Blcmshield will sail a Chinese sailing ship around the world. This morning at 7 AM, it set sail from the Hengchangxiang Wharf in Pudong. The ship has a total of seven people, all of whom have navigation knowledge and experience, and are young and strong, unafraid of difficulties. This trip is via Hong Kong and the Nanyang Islands, eastward to America via Australia, expected to take seven months, and then return east via Europe and Africa. Of the seven people, one is Chinese, two are American, two are Russian, and one each from England and France. The details are as follows:

Number of People on Board 149

The ship has a total of seven people on board. Ship owner John Blcmshield (American), Director Laring Farnswortt (American), crew members Gomkaliaze (Russian), Lhehladze (Russian), Ruffro (French), Carter (English), and Chinese head sailor Li Yinhe. Each person wears a sailor's hat with the four golden embroidered Chinese characters "New Horizon."

Equipment of the Ship 150

The ship is named "New Horizon," 65 feet long and 13 feet wide, all black with a red deck and bow. It is in the form of a sea fishing boat. The bow is the cargo hold, storing food and utensils. The middle section is the bedroom, divided into two rooms, the front room being two bedrooms, the back room being the dining room. The four walls are painted red. The tables, chairs, and utensils are all Chinese furniture. The stern is the kitchen. Cooking and lighting are done with kerosene. Provisions, milk, canned food, are sufficient for two months' use. Even a large box of cigarettes is prepared. The compass and radio are located in the central cabin. There are a total of three masts at the front and rear. The sails and hull are very strong. Sailing relies entirely on wind power.

Sailing Route 151

Departing this morning at 7 AM, sailing straight to Hong Kong. After adding supplies in Hong Kong, it will head south through Little Luzon, the Nanyang Islands, Java, Australia's Palmerston, York Peninsula, the Fiji Islands, the Phoenix Islands, Honolulu, the Hawaiian Islands, and San Francisco. Then, via the Panama Canal, the Bahama Islands, to New York. The estimated time is seven months. After a short rest, the return date will be set, and it will return to Asia via Europe and Africa. The exact date is difficult to predict. All islands, large and small, along the way will be visited.

Reader's Advice

Charity 162

丨Letter from Mr. Liu Wenjun丨

The rapidly advancing wheel of the world is trapped in the flood of unemployment. The wheel continues to advance, but the flood of unemployment flows like a waterfall! This is a major problem, and people should be concerned as if facing a great disaster, although it is something that no one can solve immediately. A major eruption and destruction are imminent. Not only have the planes and guns of the Japanese shattered people's illusions, but also the current crisis should awaken people!

Shanghai is a vibrant and ever-changing society, and also the place where the waterfall flows most rapidly. We can no longer blindly believe that the vitality of a prosperous city will revitalize people's flowers, nor should we dream of unattainable aspirations! To understand society, one must look into the depths and dark corners of society! It is in these depths and dark corners that the greatest force pushing the wheel of history is hidden!

These depths and dark corners are filled with the unemployed. Sir, let us look at our suffering compatriots and whether they are being saved. In southern Shanghai, there are several shelters set up during the winter, organized by charitable groups. These are certainly places for our suffering compatriots to seek refuge from the cold. The shelters are overcrowded with ordinary people, and many staff members wear forgiving faces to bestow happiness on the charitable donors. Whether they can wholeheartedly fulfill their mission, I will not say here, but the whips they use to drive the common people are often in their hands. They summon common people last year and dismiss common people this year, although the arrival and departure are equally freezing. (It is said that the cold shelters will be disbanded during this freezing time, or have already been disbanded.) Now, with the spring snow falling and the cold air no less than in the severe winter, we can once again see our suffering compatriots on the streets and in the alleys!

Sir, a small number of people in society enjoy not working, while the majority of the people become refugees. Fortunately, they can still rely on the blessings of the "rich people" to be slightly sheltered from the cold. However, "the arrival and departure are equally freezing." I truly do not understand why the charitable donors, who are also rich people, must make us, this group of suffering compatriots, experience the cruel coldness of heavy snowfall! The rich show mercy to the poor, and the poor should have what kind of gratitude, but the heavy snow when leaving the shelter chills their enthusiasm for gratitude!

I want to ask the following of you, sir: "The current environment will have a major destruction, and the unemployed are at the center of it, and the problem of unemployment will only be solved after the destruction. Charity is merely a palliative." Is my guess and prediction correct? What are your views on the unemployment problem? And what are your comments on the attitude of today's charitable donors? These are the answers I seek!

The unemployment problem is the prerequisite for all problems, and the charity problem is the product of the unemployment problem. These are all important, so please express your opinions!

Answer: The question you raise is very important and can be said to be the most central issue in today's society. I offer the following reply based on my observations: 1. Unemployment is a common phenomenon in today's society, and it is also the inevitable result of today's society, i.e., capitalist society. This problem is certainly very serious in China, but it is equally serious in Europe and America. As you say in your letter, "The current environment will have a major destruction... The problem of unemployment will only be solved after the destruction." However, this destruction is only the destruction of a small number of people, namely the old system, the old organization, the destruction of people who simply enjoy not working. 2. Our attitude toward charitable organizations is the same as yours, because charitable organizations, at their highest evaluation, are nothing more than a head-fixing-headache, foot-fixing-foot ache solution. Honestly, when people are unemployed, have no work, no food, no clothes, and watch their wives and children "weep with hunger and cry with cold," then they become thieves and bandits. What other way can they go? However, we are equally opposed to it. Why? Because this action cannot solve the fundamental problem of this social phenomenon, and it makes the general poor "hooligans." As a result, they lose their revolutionary spirit and instead become a major obstacle to the future, because their lives become romanticized and they develop the mentality of "drink today, forget tomorrow." The phenomenon in Shanghai is very obvious. You said, "Charitable organizations are the product of the unemployment problem," which is correct; however, if you say, "The unemployment problem is the prerequisite for all problems," then there is room for discussion. Because to solve the unemployment problem, one cannot simply think about the unemployment problem itself, that is, the eyes of the unemployed masses cannot only focus on the economic struggle, but must also focus on the improvement of politics.

In the article "Sympathy for Mr. Ren Wangtong's Views on Suicide" in this column on the 17th, the phrase "cannot achieve success" is missing after "extremely solid fighting organization" in the thirty-ninth line. This is hereby corrected.

Summary 164

The gold market, which fell the day before due to the emergence of Guangdong merchants, suddenly rebounded sharply yesterday with vigorous covering. The market situation was extremely chaotic. The United States' Plan for Silver

The Ministry of Finance is allowed to purchase 40 million taels of silver per month, with the purchase price limited to 4 to 7.5 horns per tael. 172

Washington, 17th: The Coinage Committee of the House of Representatives, the designated review committee, agreed to the proposal to implement increased use of silver, which (or tomorrow) will be submitted to the Coinage Committee. The plan is to allow the Ministry of Finance to purchase 40 million taels of silver per month for use in silver coins. A type of silver coin coupon will be issued for silver coins to be used, and the value of the silver purchased will be limited from four to seven and a half corners. Appendix: The House Silver Coinage Committee announced on February 14 that it would collect various silver coinage proposals to establish a silver coinage with a ratio of one-sixteenth, and designated a review committee to plan the silver reserves for the silver coins. The chairman of the Coinage Committee also said that the main task of the review committee is to regulate the relationship between silver reserves and the treasury and to prevent the treasury from damaging the abandonment of silver.
